<div id="S001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec-type_intro NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i2" class="section-heading-2">1. Introduction</h2>
 <p>As a result of the digital implementation of a controller, the control variable is quantised. Since the quantisation error of the digital-to-analogue conversion (DAC) can be made small by using appropriate hardware, a controller synthesis assuming real-valued control inputs is still possible without sacrificing stability or performance as long as an appropriate robustness of the approach is guaranteed. However, if for technical reasons, only a coarse quantisation of the system input is possible, the assumption of a real-valued input does not hold any longer in the step of the controller synthesis. Moreover, processes exist where the control input is integer-valued. Examples are furnaces with a discrete set of individual burners or heating elements that are either switched on or off. In other applications, variable feeds are realised by a dynamically changing number of opened solenoid valves. In such cases, the discrete nature of the process has to be considered in the design of the controller.</p>
 <p>To illustrate the difference, Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0001">1</a> shows the result of an optimal open-loop control for a reference tracking problem, which will be discussed in more detail in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S004">4</a>. The system is assumed to be of second order, with a 16-step input quantisation; that is, a 4-bit resolution. An optimal control with an underlying integer-restricted optimisation provides significantly better results compared to a control based on a real-valued optimisation and a subsequent rounding strategy, as seen in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0001">1</a>.</p>
 <p>For an open-loop control problem, and starting from a real-valued formulation, the transfer to an integer-restricted domain is straightforward because it only requires an additional constraint in the original optimisation task. The adapted optimisation will give a solution with an unknown gap to the (hypothetical) real-valued solution, which is irrelevant for the open-loop case.</p>
 <div class="figure figureViewer" id="F0001">
  <div class="hidden figureViewerArticleInfo">
   <span class="figViewerTitle">Norm-optimal iterative learning control in an integer-valued control domain</span>
   <div class="articleAuthors articleInfoSection">

 </div>
 <div class="hidden rs_skip" id="fig-description-F0001">
  <p class="captionText"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 1. </span> Reference tracking example with a 4-bit actuation using optimal open-loop control with subsequent rounding and integer-constrained optimisation. For more information, see Section&nbsp;<a href="#S004">4</a>.</p>
 </div>
 <div class="hidden rs_skip" id="figureFootNote-F0001">
  <div class="figureFootNote-F0001"></div>
 </div>
 <p></p>
 <p>For a closed-loop control formulation, the computational cost to actually solve the integer optimisation problem is very high, which may prohibit a real-time implementation. Nevertheless, first approaches have been published. Axehill et&nbsp;al.&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0004" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>) solved a discrete control problem in the context of model predictive control (MPC). Bürger et&nbsp;al.&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0008" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>) discussed an MPC setup for a nonlinear switching system, and Arnold et&nbsp;al.&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0003" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2020</a></span>) compared two approaches for binary iterative learning control (ILC).</p>
 <p>In this article, we will focus on norm-optimal ILC for cyclic processes as introduced by Amann et&nbsp;al.&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0002" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1998</a></span>). This scheme exploits the periodicity of the process to improve a control trajectory from cycle to cycle. The remaining control error and the applied actuation from an entire cycle are used to calculate an optimal control input for the upcoming cycle by minimising an appropriate cost function. In an unconstrained case, depending on the cost function and the model considered, the optimisation task in each cycle can be solved analytically. This makes the approach very efficient and suitable for real-time application. Moreover, the analytical solution allows for a distinct convergence and stability analysis of the closed loop.</p>
 <p>These advantages do not apply to the ILC with an integer-constrained optimisation that is considered here and that should meet the following performance criteria, which will be fulfilled with the <i>optimal set synthesis</i> introduced in this contribution:</p>
 <p><i>Performance criteria:</i> An integer-valued ILC should ideally ensure that</p>
 <ul class="NLM_list NLM_list-list_type-bullet">
  <li><p class="inline">the smallest upper bound of the cost function is guaranteed,</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">the norm of the control error <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0001.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0001.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         e
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi>
         k
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span> decreases monotonically over the cycles, and</p></li>
  <li><p class="inline">each control step is associated with a deterministic computational cost.</p></li>
 </ul>
 <p></p>
 <p>The organisation of this work is as follows: Section&nbsp;<a href="#S002">2</a> briefly summarises the idea of a conventional norm-optimal ILC and provides some convergence results before the integer-constrained approaches are investigated. We then shortly recapitulate two of our previously introduced approaches to improve convergence of an integer-valued ILC and discuss their properties with respect to the stated performance criteria. Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003">3</a> then introduces the optimal set controller synthesis method that ensures an upper bound for the control error as well as a deterministic computational effort during each optimisation step. For evaluation, different approaches are compared in a simulation example in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S004">4</a> before we conclude in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S005">5</a>.</p>
</div>
<div id="S002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i4" class="section-heading-2">2. Real-valued and integer-valued norm-optimal iterative learning control</h2>
 <p>Different methods of designing an ILC have been proposed (Ahn et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0001" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2007</a></span>; Bristow et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0006" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2006</a></span>; Hätönen et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0011" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2004</a></span>; Xu,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0024" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2011</a></span>). Since we will use ILC in an integer setting, this section only focuses on the so-called norm-optimal iterative learning control introduced by Amann et&nbsp;al.&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0002" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1998</a></span>), which can be expanded to a general constrained case (Chu &amp;&nbsp;Owens,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0009" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2010</a></span>; Mishra et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0013" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2011</a></span>; Peng et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0017" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2016</a></span>).</p>
 <p>Because an integer-valued situation has not yet been considered and to highlight the challenges, we start with the unconstrained, real-valued case and recapitulate some properties.</p>
 <div id="S002-S2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">

    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0036.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <msub>
      <mrow>
       <mi mathvariant="bold">
        W
       </mi>
      </mrow>
      <mrow>
       <mi>
        U
       </mi>
      </mrow>
     </msub>
    </math></span>, the filter <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0037.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0037.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       P
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </math></span>, often also named the Q-filter, results in the identity matrix. Hence, the control trajectory is adjusted proportionally to the control error of the last cycle for this case with the learning gain <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0038.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0038.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       L
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </math></span>.</p><statement id="st6" content-type="remark">
   Remark 2.4 
   <p>The weight <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0039.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0039.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span> was introduced to increase the robustness of the approach and to provide a more cautious change of the control trajectory towards a converged solution. By decreasing this weight, the converged solution will be reached in fewer cycles. For <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0040.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0040.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub><mo>
       =
      </mo><msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub><mo>
       =
      </mo><mrow>
       <mn mathvariant="bold">
        0
       </mn>
      </mrow>
     </math></span> and <i>nu</i> = <i>ny</i>, the inverse-based ILC results (Bristow et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0006" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2006</a></span>), which reach the global optimum in a single iteration.</p>
  </statement>
  <p>The computational complexity to compute the control trajectory in each cycle, according to&nbsp;(<a href="#M0008">8</a>), is <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>

    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0041.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="script">
       O
      </mi>
     </mrow><mo>
      (
     </mo><msub>
      <mi>
       n
      </mi>
      <mi>
       u
      </mi>
     </msub><mo>
      ⋅
     </mo><msub>
      <mi>
       n
      </mi>
      <mi>
       u
      </mi>
     </msub><mo>
      )
     </mo>
    </math></span> if <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0042.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0042.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       P
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </math></span> and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0043.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0043.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       L
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </math></span> are precalculated in advance and basic matrix vector multiplication is applied for the control trajectory update in each cycle. More advanced ILC update calculation can be exploited to reduce the computational burden to <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0044.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0044.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="script">
       O
      </mi>
     </mrow><mo>
      (
     </mo><msub>
      <mi>
       n
      </mi>
      <mi>
       u
      </mi>
     </msub><mo>
      )
     </mo>
    </math></span> (van Zundert et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0022" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2016</a></span>). However, the computational cost increases significantly if a constraint restricts the solution space to a domain of allowable real-valued inputs or, as a special case, to an integer domain, because an analytic solution such as&nbsp;(<a href="#M0008">8</a>) cannot be given anymore. The latter case is considered next with an integer-valued input.</p>
 </div>
 <div id="S002-S2002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i18">2.2. Integer-valued control input</h3>
  <p>To distinguish between integer-valued (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0045.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0045.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       u
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </math></span>) and real-valued control (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0046.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0046.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">
      μ
     </mi>
    </math></span>) inputs, we will use a different notation <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0047.gif" alt="">

     <msub>
      <mrow>
       <mi mathvariant="bold">
        u
       </mi>
      </mrow>
      <mrow>
       <mi>
        k
       </mi>
      </mrow>
     </msub><mo>
      ∈
     </mo><msup>
      <mrow>
       <mi mathvariant="double-struck">
        N
       </mi>
      </mrow>
      <mrow>
       <msub>
        <mi>
         n
        </mi>
        <mi>
         u
        </mi>
       </msub>
      </mrow>
     </msup>
    </math></span> for the control inputs that are restricted to the integer domain.</p>
  <p>Similar to a conventional ILC, the minimum of the cost function&nbsp;(<a href="#M0001">1</a>) has to be calculated in every iteration <i>k</i>, now with <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

  </statement>
  <p>The objective function&nbsp;(<a href="#M0014">14</a>) is similar to the cost function&nbsp;(<a href="#M0001">1</a>), and algorithms exist that can solve such an integer-constraint QP. A widely used approach is the so-called <i>branch-and-bound</i> method, compare with Morrison et&nbsp;al.&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0014" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2016</a></span>).</p><statement content-type="assumption" id="st8">
   Assumption 2.2 
   <p>In all further considerations, we assume that applying the <i>branch-and-bound</i> algorithm results in the optimal solution.</p>
  </statement>
  <p>A detailed overview on the convergence behaviour of <i>branch-and-bound</i> optimisation schemes can be found in Kannan and&nbsp;Barton&nbsp;(<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0012" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>). In contrast to QP&nbsp;1, even with additional restrictions that reduce the feasible set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0052.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0052.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="script">
       U
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </math></span>, solving the Integer-QP (IQP)&nbsp;2 can be computationally too expensive in an application since the <i>branch-and-bound</i> algorithm has to explore the entire solution space in a worst-case scenario. Moreover, the restrictions can influence the convergence behaviour of the ILC.</p>
 </div>
 <div id="S002-S2003" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i25">2.3. Convergence analysis</h3>
  <p>Again, the analysis is considered for the unconstrained, real-valued case first before properties for the integer-valued setup are derived. We focus here on stability, uniqueness of the solution, and monotonicity in both cases.</p>
 </div>
 <div id="S002-S2004" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">

  <p>As the convergence condition&nbsp;(<a href="#M0020">20</a>) relies on the update law&nbsp;(<a href="#M0008">8</a>), obtained by the analytical calculation of the minimum of the cost function, it is evident that this definition is not suitable when a constrained optimisation is necessary to obtain the control trajectory in each cycle. This will be considered next.</p>

  </statement><statement id="st21" content-type="lemma">
   Lemma 2.2 
   <p>An integer-valued norm-optimal ILC with a branch-and-bound optimisation method converges to a final state.</p>
  </statement><statement id="st22" content-type="proof">

   <p></p>
   <p>Alternatively, we assume that in addition to (a) in at least one step <i>j</i> from cycle to cycle, <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>

     </math></span>. Following a similar argument as above, a periodic behaviour can be ruled out likewise.</p>
   <p>As a result, a cyclic behaviour in the control input does not occur. This is true as well for the control error. For <i>m</i>&gt;1, an identical control error <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   <p>Finally, the optimiser will guarantee that the positive definite cost function either decreases towards 0 or stays constant in a converged state, thereby eliminating unstable behaviour in the cycle domain. As a result, an exhaustive search of the complete <i>branch-and-bound</i> tree has to be performed to find the optimal solution <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0099.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0099.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         u
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mi>
        k
       </mi>
      </msub>
     </math></span>, and convergence to a final state is shown.</p>
  </statement>

  <div id="S002-S2006-S3001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3">
   <h4 class="section-heading-4" id="_i51">2.6.1. Weight adaptation</h4>
   <p>A first intuitive solution is the adaptation of the weight <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0131.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0131.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span> to reduce the penalisation of the shift <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0132.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0132.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Δ
      </mi><msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         u
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mi>
        k
       </mi>
      </msub>
     </math></span>, compare Remark&nbsp;2.7. In a real-valued norm-optimal ILC, this results in a more aggressive change of the control trajectory, see Remark&nbsp;2.4. Here, after reaching a cycle for which the control trajectory according to Lemma&nbsp;2.3 is no longer changed, a reduction allows for further modifications of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0133.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0133.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mrow>
       <mi mathvariant="bold">
        u
       </mi>
      </mrow>
     </math></span>. It is assumed, though, that initially, far off the optimum, a <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0134.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0134.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub><mo>
       ≠
      </mo><mrow>
       <mn mathvariant="bold">
        0
       </mn>
      </mrow>
     </math></span> is applied to avoid large control moves, which may lead to possible overshoots or oscillations as the linear model is often only valid in the vicinity of an operating point. Also, due to the occurrence of non-periodic disturbances, large changes <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0135.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0135.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Δ
      </mi><msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         u
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi>
         k
        </mi>
        <mo>
         +
        </mo>
        <mn>
         1
        </mn>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span> are undesirable, which is likewise prohibited by the action of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0136.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0136.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span>.</p>
   <p>When the solution of QP&nbsp;3 does not change anymore between two cycles, a discounting factor <i>p</i>&lt;1 is used to attenuate the weight: <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_m0037.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_m0037.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div"><span id="M0037" class="disp-formula-label">(37) </span></span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msubsup>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi>
         k
        </mi>
        <mo>
         +
        </mo>
        <mn>
         1
        </mn>
       </mrow>
      </msubsup><mo>
       =
      </mo><msubsup>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mi>
        k
       </mi>
      </msubsup><mo>
       ⋅
      </mo><mi>
       p
      </mi>
     </math><span class="mathjaxLabel"><span class="disp_formula_label_div"><span id="M0037" class="disp-formula-label">(37) </span></span></span></span>To illustrate the idea, the optimisation is compared to a problem in which a change in the control trajectory is not penalised at all and that is based on a cost function characterised only by the matrix in&nbsp;(<a href="#M0036">36</a>).   <div id="S002-S2006-S3002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3">
   <h4 class="section-heading-4" id="_i54">2.6.2. Parallel real-valued ILC</h4>
   <p>An alternative ad-hoc approach to improve convergence to the best possible solution is the implementation of an additional real-valued ILC in parallel with similar weights. The real-valued ILC provides a virtual control trajectory <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0156.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">

       </mrow>

   <div class="hidden rs_skip" id="figureFootNote-F0003">
    <div class="figureFootNote-F0003"></div>
   </div>
   <p></p>
   <p>Note that during these five cycles, the same integer-valued control input would be applied to the system so that the speed of convergence is substantially slowed and the evolution of the control error would only be non-increasing instead of decreasing, see second performance criterion. However, if there are unused computational resources, the cycles where the integer-valued control input does not change can be solved virtually in one real-time cycle. Nevertheless, a non-constant number of solutions to the real-valued subproblem prohibits a deterministic computational cost (criterion 3). Here, it should be pointed out that we focus on applications where there is not arbitrary time available for resetting a process. Rather, we look at situations such as in a pulsed detonation engine, where detonations have to follow one after the other without much time for recomputing a new firing pattern (Rähse et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0018" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2018</a></span>; Schäpel et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0021" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2016</a></span>; Wolff &amp;&nbsp;King,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0023" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2019</a></span>).</p>
   <p>In contrast to the first discussed approach with an adaptive weight <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0166.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0166.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="bold">
         W
        </mi>
       </mrow>
       <mrow>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">
         Δ
        </mi>
        <mi>
         U
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span>, the second approach does not necessarily converge to the integer control trajectory obtained by QP&nbsp;4, meaning the open-loop optimal solution.</p>
  </div>
 </div>
</div>
<div id="S003" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i60" class="section-heading-2">3. Controller synthesis based on an optimal set</h2>
 <p>For the two introduced approaches, we implicitly assumed that solving the QP gives the optimal solution without fail. For a simulation study, this is a valid assumption as conventional IQP solver like <i>Gurobi</i> (Gurobi Optimization,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0010" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2020</a></span>) or <i>CPLEX</i> (Bliek et&nbsp;al.,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2014</a></span>) are reliable even for sizeable control optimisation problems. However, the computational effort to solve IQPs is very high and non-deterministic as a solution algorithm relies on a prior unknown exploration of a search tree. Consequently, an alternative approach is necessary that ensures reduced and deterministic computational costs, which is a prerequisite for a real-time application.</p>
 <p>A leverage point is, again, the penalisation of the change of the control trajectory <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0167.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0167.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi mathvariant="normal">
     Δ
    </mi><msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       u
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mrow>
      <mi>
       k
      </mi>
      <mo>
       +
      </mo>
      <mn>
       1
      </mn>
     </mrow>
    </msub>
   </math></span>. The penalisation aims at avoiding overly large changes in the control trajectory. So the range of possible control trajectories for the next cycle is limited, since solutions far away from the current control input will result in larger cost function values for the considered quadratic optimisation problems. Nevertheless, these solutions are still feasible considering QP&nbsp;3, and therefore, they might be explored during the solution of the IQP. Hence, it seems reasonable to replace the penalisation with an additional constraint that reduces the solution space of the QP and, consequently, also the computational cost.</p>
 <p><b>Quadratic program (QP) 6 (QP in a restricted set</b> <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0168.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="script">
       S
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mrow>
      <mi>
       k
      </mi>
      <mo>
       +
      </mo>
      <mn>
       1
      </mn>
     </mrow>
    </msub>
   </math></span>): In each cycle, the control trajectory is given by the solution of the&nbsp;QP <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">

 <p>Qaudratic program&nbsp;6 is the basis for the <i>optimal set controller synthesis</i> introduced below. The idea is to find a set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   </math></span> such that the smallest worst-case upper bound for the cost function is guaranteed and that a solution can be reached in a fixed number of optimisation steps in a cycle.     </mo><mi>

    </mo>
   </math></span>. In contrast, an alternative set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">

 <p></p>
 <p>Solving the QP in each iteration only requires five evaluations of the cost function in this example; thus, the computational effort increases linearly (with order <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0203.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0203.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mi>
     O
    </mi><mo>
     (
    </mo><mi>
     n
    </mi><mo>
     )
    </mo>
   </math></span>) with the number <i>n</i> of elements in the set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0204.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0204.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="script">
      V
     </mi>
    </mrow>
   </math></span>. Nevertheless, the initial control trajectory influences the performance of this approach. Depending on the initial control <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0205.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0205.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       u
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mn>
      0
     </mn>
    </msub>
   </math></span> or error trajectory <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0206.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0206.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       e
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mn>
      0
     </mn>
    </msub>
   </math></span>, the ILC-controlled plant might end in different converged solutions <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0207.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0207.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       u
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mi>
      N
     </mi>
    </msub>
   </math></span>, resulting in corresponding final costs <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0208.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0208.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mi>
      J
     </mi>
     <mi>
      N
     </mi>
    </msub>
   </math></span>, see Lemma&nbsp;2.3. As a result, for the example considered above, it cannot be stated that <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0209.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0209.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msup>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="script">
       V
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mn>
      2
     </mn>
    </msup>
   </math></span> is always better than <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0210.gif" alt="">

 <p><b>Quadratic program (QP) 7:</b> The largest local minimum for an ILC that is constrained by a set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0225.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0225.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">

     </mi>

   </math></span> according to&nbsp;(<a href="#M0045">45</a>) and&nbsp;(<a href="#M0046">46</a>) is given by <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">

 <p>The constraint&nbsp;(<a href="#M0051">51</a>) reduces the feasible solutions <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0226.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0226.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       u
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="normal">
      ∞
     </mi>
    </msub>
   </math></span> to all local minima, that is, trajectories <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0227.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0227.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       u
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="normal">
      ∞
     </mi>
    </msub>
   </math></span> where the ILC based on a set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0228.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0228.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="script">
      V
     </mi>
    </mrow>
   </math></span> might get stuck as all allowed further moves <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0229.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0229.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msup>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       v
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mi>
      i
     </mi>
    </msup>
   </math></span> would result in a higher cost. Thus, the maximisation in&nbsp;(<a href="#M0049">49</a>) yields the maximum local minima, that is, the worst-case optimal cost function value. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0006">6</a> illustrates the constraint&nbsp;(<a href="#M0051">51</a>) again for the two-dimensional example and the set given in&nbsp;(<a href="#M0047">47</a>).</p>

 <p>Note that the optimisation in NLP&nbsp;(1), in contrast to all previous quadratic optimisations, is highly nonlinear and is, therefore, much more complex to solve (Burer &amp;&nbsp;Letchford,&nbsp;<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0007" data-reflink="_i92 _i93" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2012</a></span>). However, NLP&nbsp;(1) can be solved prior to the actual operation during the controller synthesis and convergence of the online applied QP&nbsp;6 is not touched.</p>Remark 3.2

   </math></span> in&nbsp;(<a href="#M0028">28</a>) is one of the feasible solutions from QP&nbsp;7. Consequently, reducing the maximum control error in NLP&nbsp;1 also reduces the area of the final control error.</p>
 <p>The main advantage of solving QP&nbsp;6 with the moves determined by NLP&nbsp;1 is the deterministic computational effort in each cycle or iteration. Each iteration only requires the evaluation and comparison of <i>n</i> quadratic matrix expressions that represent the cost function. The second benefit of this optimal set synthesis (OSS) is the upper bound for the control performance <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0247.gif" alt="">

   <math>
    <msub>
     <mi>
      J
     </mi>
     <mo>

     </mo>
    </msub>
   </math></span> itself, as applying the obtained set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0248.gif" alt="">

   <math>
    <mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="script">
      V
     </mi>
    </mrow>
   </math></span> to the ILC setup will guarantee a worst-case control performance according to <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0249.gif" alt="">

   <math>
    <msub>
     <mi>
      J
     </mi>
     <mo>
      +
     </mo>
    </msub>
   </math></span>. Finally, the optimisation-based ILC in the QP&nbsp;6 guarantees a monotonic behaviour with which all performance criteria specified above are met.</p>

We then compare the results with the two methods discussed in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S002-S2006">2.6</a>.  <p>The adaptive weight approach also reaches the same solution, but it takes close to 200 cycles. This slower convergence is due to the necessary adaptation of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0270.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0270.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       W
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Δ
      </mi>
      <mi>
       U
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </msub>
   </math></span>. The stair-like evolution for this ILC setup in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0007">7</a> indicates that it often takes a few cycles to properly adjust the weight. Nevertheless, a smaller initial weight <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0271.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0271.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="bold">
       W
      </mi>
     </mrow>
     <mrow>
      <mi mathvariant="normal">
       Δ
      </mi>
      <mi>
       U
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </msub>
   </math></span> or a more aggressive adaptation by means of a reduced <i>p</i> can speed up the convergence of this setup but might lead to unfavourable oscillations.</p>
 <p>In contrast, the implementation with an additional real-valued ILC does not ultimately lead to the optimal control trajectory, as argued from a theoretical point of view in Section&nbsp;<a href="#S002-S2006">2.6</a>. Even though it results in a similar order of magnitude for the control error, the converged control trajectory is not optimal with respect to the 2-norm of the error over one cycle, that is, the solution of QP&nbsp;4. Also, the corresponding error evolution given in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0007">7</a> shows that this approach does not necessarily guarantee a monotonic learning behaviour. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0008">8</a> displays the different control trajectories applied for the converged cycle.</p>

   </math></span>. The parallel ILC setup gives a final result similar to the OSS, after more cycles, but again does not show monotonic learning behaviour.</p>
 <p>As already described, a main advantage of the OSS is the deterministic computational effort in each iteration. However, a sound comparison with the other two approaches is difficult as the solution of the respective QPs is realised in different ways. The basic idea of the OSS is a solution space that consists of only a small number of potential solutions so that solving the QP requires only the evaluation of the cost function for each of these potential solutions. In contrast, the other two approaches require an appropriate algorithm like the <i>branch-and-bound</i> search to find the optimal solution. For that, a real-valued QP needs to be solved for every node of the search tree. However, the QP solver itself requires a certain number of simplex iterations. Therefore, we compare the number of cost function evaluation of the OSS with the number of simplex iterations of the other two approaches for each iteration. Even though the computational effort of a simplex iteration might vary dramatically from the single evaluation of the cost function, a comparison of both values shows a trend of the computational cost.</p>
 <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0010">10</a> depicts the number of QP evaluations and simplex iterations for all three setups.</p>

  <div class="hidden figureViewerArticleInfo">
   <span class="figViewerTitle">Norm-optimal iterative learning control in an integer-valued control domain</span>

    </div>

    <div class="short-legend">
     <p class="captionText"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 10. </span> Computational cost represented by the number of simplex iterations (adaptive weight ILC and parallel ILC) and number of cost function evaluations (OSS), respectively, over a number of periods.</p>
    </div>
   </div><a href="#" class="thumbnail" aria-label="thumbnail image"><img id="F0010image" src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/medium/tcon_a_1983213_f0010_oc.jpg" loading="lazy" height="340" width="500"></a>
   <div class="figureDownloadOptions">
    <a href="#" class="downloadBtn btn btn-sm" role="button">Display full size</a>
   </div>
  </div>
 </div>
 <div class="hidden rs_skip" id="fig-description-F0010">
  <p class="captionText"><span class="captionLabel">Figure 10. </span> Computational cost represented by the number of simplex iterations (adaptive weight ILC and parallel ILC) and number of cost function evaluations (OSS), respectively, over a number of periods.</p>
 </div>
 <div class="hidden rs_skip" id="figureFootNote-F0010">
  <div class="figureFootNote-F0010"></div>
 </div>The average number of simplex iterations of the adaptive weight ILC, as well as the average number for the parallel ILC, are one order of magnitude above the number of cost function evaluations for the OSS. So the computational effort for these two approaches is much greater than the effort with the OSS, which gives a similar or even better control performance. Aside from the average computational cost of a single iteration, the substantial variation between cycles is an issue concerning the real-time application of the algorithms. In particular, the number of simplex iterations of the adaptive weight ILC varies considerably with the adjustment of the weight <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
  <noscript>
   <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0280.gif" alt="">
  </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0280.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
  <math>
   <msub>
    <mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="bold">
      W

<div id="S005" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i91" class="section-heading-2">5. Conclusion</h2>
 <p>In this work, we have stated the convergence properties of an integer-valued ILC and compared them against the well-known real-valued variant. As favourable performance criteria, a smallest upper bound of the cost function, a monotonically decreasing norm of the control error, and a deterministic computational cost were proposed. Two recently presented approaches for an ILC setup in an integer domain have been recapitulated and evaluated in terms of whether all criteria were already met. Although this was not the case, insights from these investigations could be used to introduce a superior synthesis method for integer-valued ILC. For this method, two QPs were formulated. The second QP has to be solved offline to determine a feasible set of discrete actuation moves. The first QP, which has to be solved online, not only considerably reduces the computational cost but also guarantees an upper limit for the optimality of the converged control trajectory if sufficient model information is available prior to the synthesis. Additionally, the introduced optimal set synthesis ensures deterministic computational effort in each cycle of the ILC. This property makes the approach suitable for real-time applications.</p>
 <p>In future investigations, we will mainly focus on the solution of the optimisation problem&nbsp;(<a href="#M0052">52</a>) that gives the optimal set <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tcon20/2023/tcon20.v096.i01/00207179.2021.1983213/20230110/images/tcon_a_1983213_ilm0282.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">

    <mrow>
     <mi mathvariant="script">

    </mrow>
   </math></span> for a given cardinality <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
